# Deploy to Vercel

Vercel is the easiest way to deploy your Specra documentation. It's built by the creators of Next.js, so everything works perfectly out of the box.

## Why Vercel?

- **Zero configuration** - Automatic detection and setup
- **Instant deployments** - Live in under 60 seconds
- **Automatic HTTPS** - SSL certificates included
- **Edge network** - Fast loading worldwide
- **Preview deployments** - Every git push gets a URL
- **Free tier** - Generous limits for documentation sites

## Quick Deploy

<Steps>
  <Step title="Push to GitHub">
    If you haven't already, push your project to GitHub:

```bash
git init
git add .
git commit -m "Initial commit"
git remote add origin https://github.com/username/repo.git
git push -u origin main
```
  </Step>

  <Step title="Import to Vercel">
    1. Go to [vercel.com/new](https://vercel.com/new)
    2. Click "Import Git Repository"
    3. Select your documentation repository
    4. Vercel auto-detects Next.js and configures everything

    No manual configuration needed!
  </Step>

  <Step title="Deploy">
    Click "Deploy" and wait about 30-60 seconds.

    You'll get a production URL like `your-project.vercel.app`
  </Step>
</Steps>

<Callout type="success">
That's it! Your documentation is now live with automatic HTTPS and global CDN.
</Callout>

## Configuration

Vercel automatically uses these settings for Next.js projects:

| Setting | Value |
|---------|-------|
| Build Command | `npm run build` |
| Output Directory | `.next` |
| Install Command | `npm install` |
| Node Version | 20.x (latest LTS) |

### Override Settings (Optional)

If you need custom settings, create `vercel.json`:

```json
{
  "buildCommand": "npm run build",
  "outputDirectory": ".next",
  "installCommand": "npm ci",
  "framework": "nextjs",
  "regions": ["iad1"]
}
```

## Environment Variables

Add environment variables in the Vercel dashboard:

<Steps>
  <Step title="Go to Project Settings">
    Click your project ‚Üí Settings ‚Üí Environment Variables
  </Step>

  <Step title="Add Variables">
    Add your variables one by one:

```
MEILISEARCH_HOST=https://search.example.com
MEILISEARCH_API_KEY=your-search-key
NEXT_PUBLIC_GA_ID=G-XXXXXXXXXX
```

<Callout type="tip">
Variables starting with `NEXT_PUBLIC_` are exposed to the browser. Keep sensitive keys without this prefix.
</Callout>
  </Step>

  <Step title="Redeploy">
    Environment changes require a redeploy. Go to Deployments ‚Üí Click the three dots ‚Üí Redeploy.
  </Step>
</Steps>

## Custom Domain

Add your own domain to your Vercel project:

<Steps>
  <Step title="Add Domain">
    1. Go to Project Settings ‚Üí Domains
    2. Enter your domain (e.g., `docs.example.com`)
    3. Click "Add"
  </Step>

  <Step title="Configure DNS">
    Vercel shows you the DNS records to add. Typically:

**For subdomain (docs.example.com):**
```
Type: CNAME
Name: docs
Value: cname.vercel-dns.com
```

**For apex domain (example.com):**
```
Type: A
Name: @
Value: 76.76.21.21
```
  </Step>

  <Step title="Wait for Verification">
    DNS propagation takes 5 minutes to 48 hours (usually under an hour).

    Vercel automatically provisions an SSL certificate once DNS is verified.
  </Step>
</Steps>

## Automatic Deployments

Every git push triggers a deployment:

**Production Deployments:**
- Commits to `main` branch deploy to production
- Updates your live site automatically

**Preview Deployments:**
- Commits to other branches get preview URLs
- Pull requests get unique URLs for testing
- Perfect for reviewing changes before merging

### Preview URLs

Each preview deployment gets a unique URL:

```
your-project-git-feature-branch-username.vercel.app
```

Share this with your team to review changes before going live.

## Deployment Settings

### Branch Configuration

Control which branches deploy:

1. Go to Settings ‚Üí Git
2. Set Production Branch (usually `main`)
3. Enable/disable preview deployments for other branches

### Deployment Protection

Protect production deployments:

```json
{
  "git": {
    "deploymentEnabled": {
      "main": true,
      "staging": "preview"
    }
  }
}
```

## Performance Optimization

Vercel automatically optimizes your deployment:

- **Edge caching** - Static files cached globally
- **Image optimization** - Next.js Image component optimized automatically
- **Compression** - Gzip/Brotli compression enabled
- **HTTP/2** - Faster multiplexed connections

### Analytics

Enable Vercel Analytics for free:

1. Go to Analytics tab
2. Click "Enable Analytics"
3. Add the Analytics component to your layout

```tsx
// app/layout.tsx
import { Analytics } from '@vercel/analytics/react'

export default function RootLayout({ children }) {
  return (
    <html>
      <body>
        {children}
        <Analytics />
      </body>
    </html>
  )
}
```

## CI/CD Integration

Vercel acts as your CI/CD pipeline:

**What runs on every deployment:**
- `npm install` (dependencies)
- `npm run build` (Next.js build)
- Automatic checks and validations
- Deploy to edge network

### GitHub Integration

Vercel comments on pull requests with:
- Preview deployment URL
- Build logs
- Performance insights

### Build Logs

View detailed build logs:
1. Go to Deployments
2. Click any deployment
3. View the Building section for logs

## Troubleshooting

### Build Fails

**Check Node version:**
Ensure you're using Node 18+. Add to `package.json`:

```json
{
  "engines": {
    "node": ">=18.0.0"
  }
}
```

**Clear build cache:**
1. Go to Settings ‚Üí General
2. Scroll to Build & Development Settings
3. Clear build cache

### Environment Variables Not Working

- Check variable names (case-sensitive)
- Prefix client-side variables with `NEXT_PUBLIC_`
- Redeploy after changing variables

### Custom Domain Not Working

- Verify DNS records are correct
- Wait for DNS propagation (check with `dig` or `nslookup`)
- Ensure CNAME points to `cname.vercel-dns.com`
- Check domain verification status in Vercel dashboard

## Monorepo Deployment

If your docs are in a monorepo:

1. Set Root Directory in project settings
2. Point to your docs folder (e.g., `apps/docs`)
3. Vercel builds only that directory

```json
{
  "buildCommand": "cd ../.. && npm run build:docs",
  "outputDirectory": ".next"
}
```

## Best Practices

**Use preview deployments** - Test changes before merging to main

**Enable branch protection** - Require preview deployment success before merging

**Set up notifications** - Get Slack/email alerts for deployment status

**Monitor analytics** - Track page views and performance

**Use edge config** - Store feature flags and config at the edge for instant updates

## Pricing

Vercel's free tier includes:
- Unlimited deployments
- 100GB bandwidth/month
- Automatic HTTPS
- Preview deployments
- Analytics (basic)

This is usually enough for documentation sites. Upgrade to Pro if you need:
- More bandwidth
- Advanced analytics
- Password protection
- Enterprise support

## Next Steps

  <Card
    icon="github"
    title="GitHub Pages"
    description="Deploy as static site to GitHub Pages"
    href="/docs/v1.0.0/deployment/github-pages"
  />
  <Card
    icon="globe"
    title="Netlify"
    description="Alternative static hosting platform"
    href="/docs/v1.0.0/deployment/netlify"
  />
  <Card
    icon="arrow-left"
    title="Deployment Overview"
    description="Back to deployment options"
    href="/docs/v1.0.0/deployment/overview"
  />
  <Card
    icon="zap"
    title="Performance"
    description="Optimize your documentation"
    href="/docs/v1.0.0/performance"
  />
</CardGrid>

# Getting Started with Specra

This guide will get you from zero to a fully functional documentation site in under 5 minutes. We'll cover installation, basic configuration, and writing your first page.

## Prerequisites

Before you begin, make sure you have:
- **Node.js 18 or higher** (check with `node --version`)
- A package manager: **npm** (comes with Node.js), **yarn**, or **pnpm**
- A code editor (VS Code recommended for MDX support)

## Installation

The fastest way to get started is using `create-specra`, our scaffolding tool that sets up everything for you.

<Steps>
  <Step title="Create Your Project">
    Run the create command with your project name:

    <Tabs defaultValue="npm">
      <Tab label="npm">
```bash
npx create-specra@latest my-docs
```
      </Tab>
      <Tab label="yarn">
```bash
yarn create specra my-docs
```
      </Tab>
      <Tab label="pnpm">
```bash
pnpm create specra my-docs
```
      </Tab>
    </Tabs>

    This creates a new directory called `my-docs` with all the files you need to get started.
  </Step>

  <Step title="Navigate and Install">
    Move into your new project and install dependencies:

    <Tabs defaultValue="npm">
      <Tab label="npm">
```bash
cd my-docs
npm install
```
      </Tab>
      <Tab label="yarn">
```bash
cd my-docs
yarn install
```
      </Tab>
      <Tab label="pnpm">
```bash
cd my-docs
pnpm install
```
      </Tab>
    </Tabs>

    Installation typically takes 30-60 seconds depending on your internet connection.
  </Step>

  <Step title="Start the Dev Server">
    Fire up the development server:

    <Tabs defaultValue="npm">
      <Tab label="npm">
```bash
npm run dev
```
      </Tab>
      <Tab label="yarn">
```bash
yarn dev
```
      </Tab>
      <Tab label="pnpm">
```bash
pnpm dev
```
      </Tab>
    </Tabs>

    Open [http://localhost:3000](http://localhost:3000) in your browser. You should see your documentation site with sample content!

    <Callout type="success">
    The dev server includes hot reload. Edit any MDX file and watch your changes appear instantly.
    </Callout>
  </Step>
</Steps>

## Project Structure

After running `create-specra`, here's what you get:

```txt
my-docs/
‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ app/                     # Next.js App Router
‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ layout.tsx           # Root layout with Specra providers
‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ page.tsx             # Home page
‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ docs/                # Documentation routes
‚îÇ       ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ [...slug]/       # Dynamic catch-all route
‚îÇ           ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ page.tsx     # Doc page renderer
‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ docs/                    # Your documentation content
‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ v1.0.0/             # Version folder
‚îÇ       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ about.mdx
‚îÇ       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ getting-started.mdx
‚îÇ       ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ guides/         # Folder grouping
‚îÇ           ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ _category_.json
‚îÇ           ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ writing.mdx
‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ public/                  # Static assets (images, icons)
‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ specra.config.json      # Specra configuration
‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ package.json
‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ next.config.mjs         # Next.js config (auto-managed)
‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ tailwind.config.ts      # Tailwind configuration
```

<Callout type="info">
**Important:** All documentation files must use the `.mdx` extension, not `.md`. MDX lets you use React components alongside Markdown.
</Callout>

## Your First Documentation Page

Let's create your first custom documentation page.

<Steps>
  <Step title="Create a New File">
    Inside `docs/v1.0.0/`, create a file called `hello.mdx`:

```mdx
---
title: Hello Specra
description: My first documentation page
sidebar_position: 3
---

# Hello Specra!

This is my first documentation page. I can use **bold text**,
*italic text*, and even [links](https://specra.dev).

## Features I Love

- Fast hot reload
- Beautiful components
- Simple file structure
- Zero configuration needed
```
  </Step>

  <Step title="View Your Page">
    Save the file and visit [http://localhost:3000/docs/v1.0.0/hello](http://localhost:3000/docs/v1.0.0/hello)

    You should see your new page in the sidebar and rendered beautifully in the main content area.
  </Step>

    Let's make it more interesting with a Callout component:

```mdx
---
title: Hello Specra
description: My first documentation page
sidebar_position: 3
---

# Hello Specra!

This is my first documentation page.

<Callout type="success">
  I just added an interactive component to my Markdown! No imports needed.
</Callout>

## Next Steps

```

    Save and watch it update instantly. Notice how you didn't need to import the Callout component - it's automatically available in all your MDX files.
  </Step>
</Steps>

## Understanding Frontmatter

Frontmatter is the metadata at the top of each MDX file, wrapped in triple dashes (`---`). It controls how your page appears and behaves.

### Available Fields

| Field | Type | Required | Description |
|-------|------|----------|-------------|
| `title` | string | ‚úÖ Yes | Page title shown in sidebar, browser tab, and breadcrumbs |
| `description` | string | Recommended | Brief description for SEO and social media previews |
| `sidebar_position` | number | No | Controls sidebar order (lower numbers appear first) |
| `tab_group` | string | No | Assigns page to a tab group (like "guides", "api", "components") |
| `icon` | string | No | Lucide icon name to display next to title in sidebar |
| `tags` | array | No | Tags for categorization and filtering |
| `draft` | boolean | No | Set to `true` to hide page in production builds |
| `last_updated` | string | No | Override auto-detected last updated date |

### Example Frontmatter

```mdx
---
title: Advanced Configuration
description: Deep dive into Specra configuration options
sidebar_position: 10
tab_group: guides
icon: settings
tags: [configuration, advanced, customization]
draft: false
---

# Your content starts here
```

<Callout type="tip">
Pages without `sidebar_position` are sorted alphabetically. Use this field to create a specific reading order.
</Callout>

## Organizing with Folders

Group related pages into folders for better organization. Specra automatically generates navigation from your folder structure.

### Basic Folder Structure

```txt
docs/v1.0.0/
‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ getting-started.mdx
‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ guides/
‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ installation.mdx
‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ configuration.mdx
‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ deployment.mdx
‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ api/
    ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ overview.mdx
    ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ endpoints.mdx
```

Each folder becomes a collapsible section in the sidebar.

### Category Configuration

Create a `_category_.json` file inside any folder to customize how it appears:

```json
{
  "label": "User Guides",
  "position": 2,
  "collapsible": true,
  "collapsed": false,
  "tab_group": "guides",
  "icon": "book-open"
}
```

**Options:**
- `label`: Display name in sidebar (defaults to folder name)
- `position`: Order among other folders/pages
- `collapsible`: Whether users can collapse the section
- `collapsed`: Initial collapsed state
- `tab_group`: Assign entire folder to a tab group
- `icon`: Lucide icon name

### Index Pages

Create an `index.mdx` file in a folder to provide a landing page when users click the folder name:

```txt
guides/
‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ _category_.json
‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ index.mdx          ‚Üê Landing page for /docs/v1.0.0/guides
‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ installation.mdx
‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ deployment.mdx
```

## Using Components

Specra comes with a rich library of components that are automatically available in all MDX files. No imports needed.

### Quick Examples

**Callouts for important information:**
```mdx
<Callout type="info">
  This is helpful information for your readers.
</Callout>

<Callout type="warning">
  Be careful with this setting!
</Callout>
```

**Tabs for multiple options:**
```mdx
<Tabs defaultValue="npm">
  <Tab label="npm">
    npm install specra
  </Tab>
  <Tab label="yarn">
    yarn add specra
  </Tab>
</Tabs>
```

**Steps for tutorials:**
```mdx
<Steps>
  <Step title="First Step">
    Do this first.
  </Step>
  <Step title="Second Step">
    Then do this.
  </Step>
</Steps>
```

**Cards for visual navigation:**
```mdx
<CardGrid cols={2}>
  <Card
    icon="zap"
    title="Quick Start"
    description="Get up and running fast"
    href="/docs/v1.0.0/getting-started"
  />
  <Card
    icon="book"
    title="Full Guide"
    description="Complete documentation"
    href="/docs/v1.0.0/guides"
  />
</CardGrid>
```

Explore all available components in the [Components](/docs/v1.0.0/components) section.

## Markdown Support

Specra supports all standard Markdown syntax plus GitHub Flavored Markdown extensions.

**Headings:** `#` for H1, `##` for H2, etc.
**Bold:** `**text**` or `__text__`
**Italic:** `*text*` or `_text_`
**Links:** `[text](url)`
**Images:** `![alt](url)`
**Code:** `` `inline code` ``
**Code blocks:** Triple backticks with language

**Tables:**
```markdown
| Column 1 | Column 2 |
|----------|----------|
| Data 1   | Data 2   |
```

**Task lists:**
```markdown
- [x] Completed task
- [ ] Pending task
```

**Blockquotes:**
```markdown
> This is a quote
```

# Getting Started with Specra

This guide will get you from zero to a fully functional documentation site in under 5 minutes. We'll cover installation, basic configuration, and writing your first page.

## Prerequisites

Before you begin, make sure you have:
- **Node.js 18 or higher** (check with `node --version`)
- A package manager: **npm** (comes with Node.js), **yarn**, or **pnpm**
- A code editor (VS Code recommended for MDX support)

## Installation

The fastest way to get started is using `create-specra`, our scaffolding tool that sets up everything for you.

<Steps>
  <Step title="Create Your Project">
    Run the create command with your project name:

    <Tabs defaultValue="npm">
      <Tab label="npm">
```bash
npx create-specra@latest my-docs
```
      </Tab>
      <Tab label="yarn">
```bash
yarn create specra my-docs
```
      </Tab>
      <Tab label="pnpm">
```bash
pnpm create specra my-docs
```
      </Tab>
    </Tabs>

    This creates a new directory called `my-docs` with all the files you need to get started.
  </Step>

  <Step title="Navigate and Install">
    Move into your new project and install dependencies:

    <Tabs defaultValue="npm">
      <Tab label="npm">
```bash
cd my-docs
npm install
```
      </Tab>
      <Tab label="yarn">
```bash
cd my-docs
yarn install
```
      </Tab>
      <Tab label="pnpm">
```bash
cd my-docs
pnpm install
```
      </Tab>
    </Tabs>

    Installation typically takes 30-60 seconds depending on your internet connection.
  </Step>

  <Step title="Start the Dev Server">
    Fire up the development server:

    <Tabs defaultValue="npm">
      <Tab label="npm">
```bash
npm run dev
```
      </Tab>
      <Tab label="yarn">
```bash
yarn dev
```
      </Tab>
      <Tab label="pnpm">
```bash
pnpm dev
```
      </Tab>
    </Tabs>

    Open [http://localhost:3000](http://localhost:3000) in your browser. You should see your documentation site with sample content!

    <Callout type="success">
    The dev server includes hot reload. Edit any MDX file and watch your changes appear instantly.
    </Callout>
  </Step>
</Steps>

## Project Structure

After running `create-specra`, here's what you get:

```txt

‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ layout.tsx           # Root layout with Specra providers
‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ page.tsx             # Home page
‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ docs/                # Documentation routes
‚îÇ       ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ [...slug]/       # Dynamic catch-all route
‚îÇ           ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ page.tsx     # Doc page renderer
‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ docs/                    # Your documentation content
‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ v1.0.0/             # Version folder
‚îÇ       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ about.mdx
‚îÇ       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ getting-started.mdx

## Try It Yourself

2. **Scroll to the playground** at the bottom of each endpoint
3. **Click "Send Request"** to test the API live
4. **View the response** in the JSON viewer

## About JSONPlaceholder

[JSONPlaceholder](https://jsonplaceholder.typicode.com/) is a free fake REST API for testing and prototyping. It's perfect for:

- Testing API documentation tools (like this!)
- Frontend development
- Learning HTTP methods
- Prototyping applications

<Callout type="success" title="Pro Tip">
Try modifying the request body in the POST/PUT/PATCH endpoints and see the response change!
</Callout>

## Example Integration

Here's how you might use this API in a real application:

```javascript
// Fetch all posts
async function getPosts() {
  const response = await fetch('https://jsonplaceholder.typicode.com/posts?_limit=5');
  const posts = await response.json();
  return posts;
}

// Create a new post
async function createPost(title, body) {
  const response = await fetch('https://jsonplaceholder.typicode.com/posts', {
    method: 'POST',
    headers: { 'Content-Type': 'application/json' },
    body: JSON.stringify({
      title,
      body,
      userId: 1
    })
  });
  return await response.json();
}

// Usage
const posts = await getPosts();
console.log(posts);

const newPost = await createPost('My Title', 'My Content');
console.log(newPost);
```

- Learn about [creating your own API spec](/docs/v1.0.0/api-auto-generated)
- Read the full [API Documentation Guide](/API_DOCUMENTATION.md)

# Navigation Configuration

The `navigation` section controls how users move through your documentation. Configure the sidebar, breadcrumbs, table of contents, and tab groups to create an intuitive navigation experience.

## Basic Configuration

Here's a minimal navigation setup:

```json
{
  "navigation": {
    "showSidebar": true,
    "showBreadcrumbs": true,
    "showTableOfContents": true
  }
}
```

Specra provides sensible defaults, so you only need to configure what you want to change.

## Complete Configuration

```json
{
  "navigation": {
    "showSidebar": true,
    "collapsibleSidebar": true,
    "showBreadcrumbs": true,
    "showTableOfContents": true,
    "tocPosition": "right",
    "tocMaxDepth": 3,
    "tabGroups": [
      {
        "id": "guides",
        "label": "Guides",
        "icon": "book-open"
      },
      {
        "id": "api",
        "label": "API Reference",
        "icon": "zap"
      },
      {
        "id": "components",
        "label": "Components",
        "icon": "layers"
      }
    ]
  }
}
```

## Sidebar Configuration

### showSidebar

**Type:** `boolean`
**Default:** `true`

Show or hide the sidebar navigation.

```json
{
  "navigation": {
    "showSidebar": true
  }
}
```

Set to `false` to hide the sidebar completely. Useful for landing pages or marketing sites.

### collapsibleSidebar

**Type:** `boolean`
**Default:** `true`

Allow users to collapse and expand sidebar sections.

```json
{
  "navigation": {
    "collapsibleSidebar": true
  }
}
```

When `true`, folder sections have collapse/expand arrows. When `false`, all sections are always expanded.

## Breadcrumbs

### showBreadcrumbs

**Type:** `boolean`
**Default:** `true`

Display breadcrumb navigation at the top of each page.

```json
{
  "navigation": {
    "showBreadcrumbs": true
  }
}
```

Breadcrumbs show the page's location in the documentation hierarchy:

```
Home > Guides > Getting Started
```

<Callout type="tip">
Breadcrumbs help users understand where they are and navigate back to parent sections.
</Callout>

## Table of Contents

### showTableOfContents

**Type:** `boolean`
**Default:** `true`

Display the table of contents (TOC) on documentation pages.

```json
{
  "navigation": {
    "showTableOfContents": true
  }
}
```

The TOC shows all headings on the current page with links to scroll to each section.

### tocPosition

**Type:** `"left"` or `"right"`
**Default:** `"right"`

Position the table of contents on the left or right side of the page.

```json
{
  "navigation": {
    "tocPosition": "right"
  }
}
```

**Right position (default):**
- TOC appears in the right sidebar
- Traditional documentation layout
- More reading space for content

**Left position:**
- TOC appears in the left sidebar below main navigation
- Compact layout
- Less horizontal scrolling on smaller screens

### tocMaxDepth

**Type:** `number` (1-6)
**Default:** `3`

Maximum heading level to show in the table of contents.

```json
{
  "navigation": {
    "tocMaxDepth": 3
  }
}
```

**Options:**
- `1` - Only H1 headings
- `2` - H1 and H2 headings
- `3` - H1, H2, and H3 headings (recommended)
- `4` - Up to H4
- `5` - Up to H5
- `6` - All headings

<Callout type="warning">
Setting this too high (5 or 6) can make the TOC cluttered. Most docs work best with 2 or 3.
</Callout>

## Tab Groups

Tab groups organize your documentation into logical sections with separate navigation tabs.

### Basic Tab Groups

```json
{
  "navigation": {
    "tabGroups": [
      {
        "id": "guides",
        "label": "Guides",
        "icon": "book-open"
      },
      {
        "id": "api",
        "label": "API Reference",
        "icon": "zap"
      }
    ]
  }
}
```

### Tab Group Properties

Each tab group has three properties:

**id** (required)
- Unique identifier for the tab group
- Used in page frontmatter: `tab_group: "guides"`
- Lowercase, no spaces

**label** (required)
- Display name shown in the tab
- Can include spaces and capitalization

**icon** (optional)
- Lucide icon name to display next to label
- Makes tabs more visual and scannable

### Assigning Pages to Tab Groups

In your MDX frontmatter, specify which tab group a page belongs to:

```mdx
---
title: Getting Started
tab_group: guides
---
```

Pages with the same `tab_group` value appear together under that tab.

### Common Tab Group Setups

**Documentation + API:**
```json
{
  "tabGroups": [
    {
      "id": "docs",
      "label": "Documentation",
      "icon": "book"
    },
    {
      "id": "api",
      "label": "API Reference",
      "icon": "code"
    }
  ]
}
```

**Guides + Components + API:**
```json
{
  "tabGroups": [
    {
      "id": "guides",
      "label": "Guides",
      "icon": "book-open"
    },
    {
      "id": "components",
      "label": "Components",
      "icon": "layers"
    },
    {
      "id": "api",
      "label": "API",
      "icon": "zap"
    }
  ]
}
```

**Multi-product documentation:**
```json
{
  "tabGroups": [
    {
      "id": "platform",
      "label": "Platform",
      "icon": "box"
    },
    {
      "id": "mobile",
      "label": "Mobile SDK",
      "icon": "smartphone"
    },
    {
      "id": "web",
      "label": "Web SDK",
      "icon": "monitor"
    }
  ]
}
```

## Available Icons

Specra uses Lucide icons. Popular choices for documentation:

**General:**
- `book` - Books, documentation
- `book-open` - Open book, reading
- `file-text` - Documents, pages
- `layout` - Layout, structure

**Technical:**
- `code` - Code, programming
- `zap` - API, fast, dynamic
- `terminal` - CLI, command line
- `database` - Database, data

**UI:**
- `layers` - Components, stack
- `palette` - Design, theming
- `settings` - Configuration
- `grid` - Layout grid

**Actions:**
- `rocket` - Launch, deployment
- `wrench` - Tools, utilities
- `shield` - Security
- `search` - Search, find

Browse all icons at [lucide.dev](https://lucide.dev/icons/)

## Sidebar Organization

### Automatic Generation

Specra automatically generates your sidebar from your file structure:

```txt
docs/v1.0.0/
‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ getting-started.mdx        ‚Üí Getting Started
‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ installation.mdx           ‚Üí Installation
‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ guides/                    ‚Üí Guides (folder)
    ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ basics.mdx            ‚Üí   Basics
    ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ advanced.mdx          ‚Üí   Advanced
```

### Controlling Order

Use `sidebar_position` in frontmatter to control page order:

```mdx
---
title: Getting Started
sidebar_position: 1
---
```

Lower numbers appear first. Pages without positions are sorted alphabetically.

### Category Configuration

Customize folder appearance with `_category_.json`:

```json
{
  "label": "User Guides",
  "position": 2,
  "collapsible": true,
  "collapsed": false,
  "icon": "book-open"
}
```

See [Writing Content](/docs/v1.0.0/writing-content) for more on organizing content.

## Examples

### Minimal Setup

Just enable the basics:

```json
{
  "navigation": {
    "showSidebar": true,
    "showBreadcrumbs": true,
    "showTableOfContents": true
  }
}
```

### Clean Layout

TOC on left, deeper headings:

```json
{
  "navigation": {
    "showSidebar": true,
    "collapsibleSidebar": true,
    "showBreadcrumbs": true,
    "showTableOfContents": true,
    "tocPosition": "left",
    "tocMaxDepth": 4
  }
}
```

### Multi-Section Documentation

With tab groups for different audiences:

```json
{
  "navigation": {
    "showSidebar": true,
    "collapsibleSidebar": true,
    "showBreadcrumbs": true,
    "showTableOfContents": true,
    "tocPosition": "right",
    "tocMaxDepth": 3,
    "tabGroups": [
      {
        "id": "getting-started",
        "label": "Getting Started",
        "icon": "rocket"
      },
      {
        "id": "developers",
        "label": "Developers",
        "icon": "code"
      },
      {
        "id": "designers",
        "label": "Designers",
        "icon": "palette"
      }
    ]
  }
}
```

## Best Practices

**Use tab groups wisely** - Don't create too many. 3-5 tabs maximum works best.

**Choose descriptive labels** - Make it obvious what's in each tab or section.

**Pick appropriate icons** - Icons should reinforce the tab's purpose.

**Set tocMaxDepth appropriately** - Most docs work best with 2 or 3 levels.

**Keep sidebar collapsible** - Let users hide sections they don't need.

**Show breadcrumbs** - They help users navigate complex documentation.

# Navigation Configuration

The `navigation` section controls how users move through your documentation. Configure the sidebar, breadcrumbs, table of contents, and tab groups to create an intuitive navigation experience.

## Basic Configuration

Here's a minimal navigation setup:

```json
{
  "navigation": {
    "showSidebar": true,
    "showBreadcrumbs": true,
    "showTableOfContents": true
  }
}
```

Specra provides sensible defaults, so you only need to configure what you want to change.

## Complete Configuration

```json
{
  "navigation": {
    "showSidebar": true,
    "collapsibleSidebar": true,
    "showBreadcrumbs": true,
    "showTableOfContents": true,
    "tocPosition": "right",
    "tocMaxDepth": 3,
    "tabGroups": [
      {
        "id": "guides",
        "label": "Guides",
        "icon": "book-open"
      },
      {
        "id": "api",
        "label": "API Reference",
        "icon": "zap"
      },
      {
        "id": "components",
        "label": "Components",
        "icon": "layers"
      }
    ]
  }
}
```

# Deploy to GitHub Pages

GitHub Pages offers free hosting for static sites, making it perfect for open source documentation. Deploy directly from your repository with GitHub Actions.

## Why GitHub Pages?

- **Free hosting** - No cost for public repositories
- **Custom domains** - Use your own domain
- **HTTPS included** - Automatic SSL certificates
- **Git-based** - Deploy from your repository
- **Version control** - Full history of your docs
- **Community trust** - Familiar platform for developers

## Prerequisites

- GitHub repository (public or private)
- Specra documentation project
- Git installed locally

## Configuration

First, configure Specra for static export.

### Without Custom Domain

For URLs like `username.github.io/repo-name`:

```json
{
  "deployment": {
    "target": "github-pages",
    "basePath": "repo-name",
    "customDomain": false
  }
}
```

<Callout type="Warning">
The `basePath` must exactly match your repository name. GitHub Pages serves from `username.github.io/repo-name`, so all assets need this prefix.
</Callout>

### With Custom Domain

For custom domains like `docs.example.com`:

```json
{
  "deployment": {
    "target": "custom-domain-static",
    "basePath": "",
    "customDomain": true
  }
}
```

Also create `public/CNAME` with your domain:

```
docs.example.com
```

## Deployment Methods

Choose your preferred deployment method:

### Method 1: GitHub Actions (Recommended)

Automatic deployment on every push to main.

<Steps>
  <Step title="Create Workflow File">
    Create `.github/workflows/deploy.yml`:

```yaml
name: Deploy to GitHub Pages

on:
  push:
    branches: [main]

permissions:
  contents: read
  pages: write
  id-token: write

concurrency:
  group: "pages"
  cancel-in-progress: false

jobs:
  build:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - name: Checkout
        uses: actions/checkout@v4

      - name: Setup Node
        uses: actions/setup-node@v4
        with:
          node-version: '20'
          cache: 'npm'

      - name: Install dependencies
        run: npm ci

      - name: Build site
        run: npm run build:export
        env:
          NODE_ENV: production

      - name: Upload artifact
        uses: actions/upload-pages-artifact@v3
        with:
          path: ./out

  deploy:
    needs: build
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    environment:
      name: github-pages
      url: ${{ steps.deployment.outputs.page_url }}
    steps:
      - name: Deploy to GitHub Pages
        id: deployment
        uses: actions/deploy-pages@v4
```
  </Step>

  <Step title="Enable GitHub Pages">
    1. Go to repository Settings ‚Üí Pages
    2. Source: **GitHub Actions**
    3. Save

No need to select a branch - the workflow handles deployment.
  </Step>

  <Step title="Push and Deploy">
```bash
git add .
git commit -m "Add GitHub Pages deployment"
git push
```

Your site deploys automatically! Check the Actions tab for progress.
  </Step>
</Steps>

### Method 2: Manual Deployment

Deploy manually using the `gh-pages` package.

<Steps>
  <Step title="Install gh-pages">
```bash
npm install --save-dev gh-pages
```
  </Step>

  <Step title="Add Deploy Script">
    Update `package.json`:

```json
{
  "scripts": {
    "deploy": "npm run build:export && gh-pages -d out"
  }
}
```
  </Step>

  <Step title="Deploy">
```bash
npm run deploy
```

This builds your site and pushes the `out` folder to the `gh-pages` branch.
  </Step>

  <Step title="Enable GitHub Pages">
    1. Go to Settings ‚Üí Pages
    2. Source: Deploy from a branch
    3. Branch: `gh-pages` / `/ (root)`
    4. Save
  </Step>
</Steps>

## Custom Domain Setup

Use your own domain with GitHub Pages:

<Steps>
  <Step title="Add CNAME File">
    Create `public/CNAME`:

```
docs.example.com
```

Update config:

```json
{
  "deployment": {
    "target": "custom-domain-static",
    "customDomain": true,
    "basePath": ""
  }
}
```
  </Step>

  <Step title="Configure DNS">
    Add DNS records at your domain provider:

**For subdomain (docs.example.com):**
```
Type: CNAME
Name: docs
Value: username.github.io
```

**For apex domain (example.com):**
```
Type: A
Name: @
Value: 185.199.108.153
Value: 185.199.109.153
Value: 185.199.110.153
Value: 185.199.111.153
```

<Callout type="tip">
Use a subdomain like `docs.example.com` - it's simpler than apex domain setup.
</Callout>
  </Step>

  <Step title="Enable HTTPS">
    After DNS propagates (can take up to 24 hours):

1. Go to Settings ‚Üí Pages
2. Check "Enforce HTTPS"
3. GitHub automatically provisions an SSL certificate
  </Step>
</Steps>

## Advanced GitHub Actions

### With Search Indexing

Index your docs in MeiliSearch during deployment:

```yaml
jobs:
  build:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4

      - name: Setup Node
        uses: actions/setup-node@v4
        with:
          node-version: '20'
          cache: 'npm'

      - name: Install dependencies
        run: npm ci

      - name: Build site
        run: npm run build:export

      - name: Index search
        run: npm run index:search
        env:
          MEILISEARCH_HOST: ${{ secrets.MEILISEARCH_HOST }}
          MEILISEARCH_API_KEY: ${{ secrets.MEILISEARCH_MASTER_KEY }}

      - name: Upload artifact
        uses: actions/upload-pages-artifact@v3
        with:
          path: ./out
```

Add secrets in Settings ‚Üí Secrets and variables ‚Üí Actions.

### Deploy on Tag

Only deploy when you create a release tag:

```yaml
on:
  push:
    tags:
      - 'v*'
```

Create and push a tag to deploy:

```bash
git tag v1.0.0
git push origin v1.0.0
```

### Multiple Environments

Deploy different branches to different GitHub Pages sites:

```yaml
on:
  push:
    branches:
      - main
      - staging

jobs:
  build:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      # ... build steps ...

      - name: Deploy to production
        if: github.ref == 'refs/heads/main'
        uses: actions/deploy-pages@v4

      - name: Deploy to staging
        if: github.ref == 'refs/heads/staging'
        # Deploy to a different repo or branch
```

## Troubleshooting

### 404 Errors on Routes

Static exports don't support dynamic routing the same way. Ensure all routes are pre-rendered.

**Solution:** Add a 404.html that redirects to index:

```html
<!DOCTYPE html>
<html>
  <head>
    <meta http-equiv="refresh" content="0;url=/" />
  </head>
  <body>
    Redirecting...
  </body>
</html>
```

### Assets Not Loading

Check your `basePath` configuration:

```bash
# View your site
open https://username.github.io/repo-name

# Check if assets load from
https://username.github.io/repo-name/_next/...
```

If assets 404, verify:
- `basePath` in config matches repo name exactly
- You're using `npm run build:export` not `npm run build`

### Custom Domain Not Working

**Check DNS propagation:**
```bash
dig docs.example.com
# Should show CNAME to username.github.io
```

**Check CNAME file:**
- Must be in `public/` folder
- Contains only your domain, no protocol
- No trailing slash

**Common issues:**
- DNS not propagated yet (wait up to 24 hours)
- CNAME file missing or incorrect
- Domain verification failed in GitHub settings

### Build Fails in Actions

**View logs:**
1. Go to Actions tab
2. Click the failed workflow
3. Expand build step to see errors

**Common fixes:**
- Increase Node version in workflow
- Clear npm cache: `npm ci --cache .npm`
- Check for missing dependencies

## Performance Tips

### Enable Caching

Cache node_modules for faster builds:

```yaml
- name: Setup Node
  uses: actions/setup-node@v4
  with:
    node-version: '20'
    cache: 'npm'
```

### Optimize Images

Pre-optimize images before committing:

```bash
npm install -D imagemin-cli

# Optimize all images
npx imagemin public/images/* --out-dir=public/images
```

### Reduce Bundle Size

Check what's in your bundle:

```bash
npm install -D @next/bundle-analyzer

ANALYZE=true npm run build:export
```

## Limits

GitHub Pages has some limits:

- **Repository size:** 1GB recommended
- **Site size:** 1GB published site
- **Bandwidth:** 100GB/month soft limit
- **Builds:** 10 per hour

These limits are generous for documentation sites.

## Migration from Other Platforms

### From Vercel

1. Update `specra.config.json` deployment section
2. Run `npm run build:export` locally to test
3. Set up GitHub Actions workflow
4. Push to trigger deployment

### From Netlify

Same process as Vercel. The static output works on both platforms.

## Best Practices

**Use GitHub Actions** - Automatic deployment on every push

**Version your docs** - Use git tags for documentation versions

**Test locally** - Run `npm run build:export && npx serve out` before pushing

**Monitor builds** - Set up notifications for failed deployments

**Use custom domain** - Professional appearance and stable URLs

**Enable HTTPS** - Always enforce HTTPS for security

## Next Steps

# Deploy to GitHub Pages

GitHub Pages offers free hosting for static sites, making it perfect for open source documentation. Deploy directly from your repository with GitHub Actions.

## Why GitHub Pages?

- **Free hosting** - No cost for public repositories
- **Custom domains** - Use your own domain
- **HTTPS included** - Automatic SSL certificates
- **Git-based** - Deploy from your repository
- **Version control** - Full history of your docs
- **Community trust** - Familiar platform for developers

## Prerequisites

- GitHub repository (public or private)
- Specra documentation project
- Git installed locally

## Configuration

First, configure Specra for static export.

### Without Custom Domain

For URLs like `username.github.io/repo-name`:

```json
{
  "deployment": {
    "target": "github-pages",
    "basePath": "repo-name",
    "customDomain": false
  }
}
```

<Callout type="Warning">
The `basePath` must exactly match your repository name. GitHub Pages serves from `username.github.io/repo-name`, so all assets need this prefix.
</Callout>

### With Custom Domain

For custom domains like `docs.example.com`:

```json
{
  "deployment": {
    "target": "custom-domain-static",
    "basePath": "",
    "customDomain": true
  }
}
```

Also create `public/CNAME` with your domain:

```
docs.example.com
```

## Deployment Methods

Choose your preferred deployment method:

### Method 1: GitHub Actions (Recommended)

Automatic deployment on every push to main.

<Steps>
  <Step title="Create Workflow File">
    Create `.github/workflows/deploy.yml`:

```yaml
name: Deploy to GitHub Pages

on:
  push:
    branches: [main]

permissions:
  contents: read
  pages: write
  id-token: write

concurrency:
  group: "pages"
  cancel-in-progress: false

jobs:
  build:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - name: Checkout
        uses: actions/checkout@v4

      - name: Setup Node
        uses: actions/setup-node@v4
        with:
          node-version: '20'
          cache: 'npm'

      - name: Install dependencies
        run: npm ci

      - name: Build site
        run: npm run build:export
        env:
          NODE_ENV: production

      - name: Upload artifact
        uses: actions/upload-pages-artifact@v3
        with:
          path: ./out

  deploy:
    needs: build
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    environment:
      name: github-pages
      url: ${{ steps.deployment.outputs.page_url }}
    steps:
      - name: Deploy to GitHub Pages
        id: deployment
        uses: actions/deploy-pages@v4
```
  </Step>

  <Step title="Enable GitHub Pages">
    1. Go to repository Settings ‚Üí Pages
    2. Source: **GitHub Actions**
    3. Save

No need to select a branch - the workflow handles deployment.
  </Step>

  <Step title="Push and Deploy">
```bash
git add .
git commit -m "Add GitHub Pages deployment"
git push
```

Your site deploys automatically! Check the Actions tab for progress.
  </Step>
</Steps>

### Method 2: Manual Deployment

Deploy manually using the `gh-pages` package.

<Steps>
  <Step title="Install gh-pages">
```bash
npm install --save-dev gh-pages
```
  </Step>

  <Step title="Add Deploy Script">
    Update `package.json`:

```json
{
  "scripts": {
    "deploy": "npm run build:export && gh-pages -d out"
  }
}
```
  </Step>

  <Step title="Deploy">
```bash
npm run deploy
```

This builds your site and pushes the `out` folder to the `gh-pages` branch.
  </Step>

  <Step title="Enable GitHub Pages">
    1. Go to Settings ‚Üí Pages
    2. Source: Deploy from a branch
    3. Branch: `gh-pages` / `/ (root)`
    4. Save
  </Step>
</Steps>

## Custom Domain Setup

Use your own domain with GitHub Pages:

<Steps>
  <Step title="Add CNAME File">
    Create `public/CNAME`:

```
docs.example.com
```

Update config:

```json
{
  "deployment": {
    "target": "custom-domain-static",
    "customDomain": true,
    "basePath": ""
  }
}
```
  </Step>

  <Step title="Configure DNS">
    Add DNS records at your domain provider:

**For subdomain (docs.example.com):**
```
Type: CNAME
Name: docs
Value: username.github.io
```

**For apex domain (example.com):**
```
Type: A
Name: @
Value: 185.199.108.153
Value: 185.199.109.153
Value: 185.199.110.153
Value: 185.199.111.153
```

<Callout type="tip">
Use a subdomain like `docs.example.com` - it's simpler than apex domain setup.
</Callout>
  </Step>

  <Step title="Enable HTTPS">
    After DNS propagates (can take up to 24 hours):

1. Go to Settings ‚Üí Pages
2. Check "Enforce HTTPS"
3. GitHub automatically provisions an SSL certificate
  </Step>
</Steps>

## Advanced GitHub Actions

### With Search Indexing

Index your docs in MeiliSearch during deployment:

```yaml
jobs:
  build:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4

      - name: Setup Node
        uses: actions/setup-node@v4
        with:
          node-version: '20'
          cache: 'npm'

      - name: Install dependencies
        run: npm ci

      - name: Build site
        run: npm run build:export

      - name: Index search
        run: npm run index:search
        env:
          MEILISEARCH_HOST: ${{ secrets.MEILISEARCH_HOST }}
          MEILISEARCH_API_KEY: ${{ secrets.MEILISEARCH_MASTER_KEY }}

      - name: Upload artifact
        uses: actions/upload-pages-artifact@v3
        with:
          path: ./out
```

Add secrets in Settings ‚Üí Secrets and variables ‚Üí Actions.

### Deploy on Tag

Only deploy when you create a release tag:

```yaml
on:
  push:
    tags:
      - 'v*'
```

Create and push a tag to deploy:

```bash
git tag v1.0.0
git push origin v1.0.0
```

### Multiple Environments

Deploy different branches to different GitHub Pages sites:

```yaml
on:
  push:
    branches:
      - main
      - staging

jobs:
  build:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      # ... build steps ...

      - name: Deploy to production
        if: github.ref == 'refs/heads/main'
        uses: actions/deploy-pages@v4

      - name: Deploy to staging
        if: github.ref == 'refs/heads/staging'
        # Deploy to a different repo or branch
```

### Build Fails in Actions

# Writing Content in Specra

Specra uses MDX (Markdown + JSX) for documentation, giving you the simplicity of Markdown with the power of React components. This guide covers everything you need to write great documentation.

## MDX Basics

MDX files look like regular Markdown but let you use React components anywhere in your content.

### Standard Markdown

All standard Markdown syntax works as expected:

**Headings:**
```markdown
# Heading 1
## Heading 2
### Heading 3
```

**Text formatting:**
```markdown
**Bold text**
*Italic text*
~~Strikethrough~~
`Inline code`
```

**Lists:**
```markdown
- Unordered list
- Another item
  - Nested item

1. Ordered list
2. Second item
   1. Nested ordered item
```

**Links and images:**
```markdown
[Link text](https://example.com)
![Alt text](/images/photo.png)
```

**Code blocks:**
````markdown
```javascript
function hello() {
  console.log("Hello, world!")
}
```
````

**Tables:**
```markdown
| Column 1 | Column 2 | Column 3 |
|----------|----------|----------|
| Data 1   | Data 2   | Data 3   |
| More     | Info     | Here     |
```

**Blockquotes:**
```markdown
> This is a quote.
> It can span multiple lines.
```

**Horizontal rules:**
```markdown
---
```

## Using Components

Components are used with JSX syntax directly in your MDX:

```mdx
<Callout type="info">
  This is a callout component!
</Callout>
```

All components are automatically available - no imports needed.

### Component Examples

**Alert readers to important information:**
```mdx
<Callout type="warning">
  Make sure to backup your data before proceeding.
</Callout>
```

**Create tabbed content:**
```mdx
<Tabs defaultValue="option1">
  <Tab label="Option 1">
    Content for the first tab
  </Tab>
  <Tab label="Option 2">
    Content for the second tab
  </Tab>
</Tabs>
```

**Guide users through steps:**
```mdx
<Steps>
  <Step title="Install dependencies">
    Run `npm install` to get started.
  </Step>
  <Step title="Configure your app">
    Edit the config file with your settings.
  </Step>
</Steps>
```

See the [Components](/docs/v1.0.0/components) section for all available components.

## Content Organization

### File Structure Best Practices

Organize files logically to make content easy to find:

```txt
docs/v1.0.0/
‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ getting-started.mdx         # Top level: essential pages
‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ installation.mdx
‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ guides/                     # Group related content
‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ _category_.json
‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ basics.mdx
‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ advanced.mdx
‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ examples/              # Further nesting for sub-topics
‚îÇ       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ _category_.json
‚îÇ       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ example-1.mdx
‚îÇ       ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ example-2.mdx
‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ api/
    ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ _category_.json
    ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ reference.mdx
```

**Tips:**
- Keep the top level for critical pages users need first
- Use folders to group related content
- Limit nesting to 2-3 levels max
- Name files descriptively (`authentication.mdx` not `auth.mdx`)

### Controlling Page Order

Use `sidebar_position` in frontmatter to control ordering:

```mdx
---
title: Installation
sidebar_position: 1
---
```

Lower numbers appear first. Pages without a position are sorted alphabetically.

For folders, use `_category_.json`:

```json
{
  "label": "Getting Started",
  "position": 1
}
```

## Writing Style Tips

Good documentation is clear, concise, and helpful. Here are some tips:

### Be Clear and Direct

**Good:**
> Click the "Save" button to save your changes.

**Bad:**
> You might want to consider clicking on the button labeled "Save" if you would like to persist your modifications to storage.

### Use Active Voice

**Good:**
> The system validates your input.

**Bad:**
> Your input is validated by the system.

### Show, Don't Just Tell

Include examples with every concept:

```mdx
## Using Environment Variables

Access environment variables in your config:

```json
{
  "env": {
    "API_URL": "https://api.example.com"
  }
}
```

Then reference them in your MDX:

```mdx
The API is available at {process.env.API_URL}
```
```

### Break Up Long Content

Use headings, lists, callouts, and components to create visual breaks:

```mdx
## Configuration Options

There are several ways to configure authentication:

### API Keys

API keys are simple but less secure.

<Callout type="warning">
  Never commit API keys to version control.
</Callout>

### OAuth 2.0

OAuth provides better security for user-facing apps.

<Steps>
  <Step title="Register your app">
    Create an app in the provider dashboard.
  </Step>
  <Step title="Configure callback URL">
    Set your redirect URI in the app settings.
  </Step>
</Steps>
```

## Working with Images

### Adding Images

Place images in the `public/` folder:

```txt
public/
‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ images/
‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ screenshot.png
‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ diagram.svg
```

Reference them in MDX:

```mdx
![Dashboard screenshot](/images/screenshot.png)
```

### Image Best Practices

**Use descriptive alt text:**
```mdx
![Login form showing email and password fields](/images/login.png)
```

**Optimize image sizes:**
- Use WebP format when possible
- Compress images before adding to repo
- Keep images under 500KB

**Use the Image component for advanced features:**
```mdx
<Image
  src="/images/hero.png"
  alt="Hero image"
  caption="The main dashboard view"
  width={800}
  height={400}
/>
```

## Code Examples

### Syntax Highlighting

Specify the language after the opening backticks:

````markdown
```javascript
const greeting = "Hello, world!"
console.log(greeting)
```

```python
def greet():
    print("Hello, world!")
```

```bash
npm install specra
```
````

Supported languages include: javascript, typescript, python, bash, json, yaml, markdown, html, css, and many more.

### Highlighting Lines

Highlight specific lines to draw attention:

````markdown
```javascript {2,4-6}
function calculateTotal(items) {
  const subtotal = items.reduce((sum, item) => sum + item.price, 0)
  const tax = subtotal * 0.1
  const shipping = 5.99
  const total = subtotal + tax + shipping
  return total
}
```
````

### File Names

Show which file the code belongs to:

````markdown
```javascript title="src/utils.js"
export function formatDate(date) {
  return date.toLocaleDateString()
}
```
````

### Use the CodeBlock Component

For more control:

```mdx
<CodeBlock
  language="javascript"
  title="src/app.js"
  highlightLines={[3, 5]}
  showLineNumbers={true}
>
{`function app() {
  const config = loadConfig()
  const server = createServer(config)
  server.listen(3000)
  console.log("Server running")
}`}
</CodeBlock>
```

## Links and Navigation

### Internal Links

Link to other pages in your docs:

```mdx
See the [Configuration guide](/docs/v1.0.0/configuration/overview) for details.
```

Use relative paths from the site root, including the version.

### External Links

External links open in a new tab automatically:

```mdx
Check out the [Next.js documentation](https://nextjs.org/docs).
```

### Anchor Links

Link to headings on the same page:

```mdx
Jump to [Installation](#installation) below.
```

Heading anchors are auto-generated from the heading text in lowercase with hyphens.

## Frontmatter Reference

Every MDX file needs frontmatter. Here's a complete example:

```mdx
---
title: Advanced Topics
description: Deep dive into advanced Specra features
sidebar_position: 10
tab_group: guides
icon: zap
tags: [advanced, configuration, optimization]
draft: false
---

# Your content starts here
```

**Required fields:**
- `title`: Page title

**Recommended fields:**
- `description`: SEO description (150-160 characters)

**Optional fields:**
- `sidebar_position`: Number for sidebar ordering
- `tab_group`: Assign to a tab group
- `icon`: Lucide icon name
- `tags`: Array of tags
- `draft`: Hide in production if true

## Advanced MDX Features

### Importing Components

While built-in components work automatically, you can import custom ones:

```mdx
import { MyCustomComponent } from '@/components/custom'

<MyCustomComponent data="example" />
```

### Using JavaScript Expressions

Embed JavaScript expressions:

```mdx
The current year is {new Date().getFullYear()}.
```

### Conditional Content

Use JavaScript for conditional rendering:

```mdx
{process.env.NODE_ENV === 'development' && (
  <Callout type="info">
    You're viewing the development version.
  </Callout>
)}
```

## Version Management

When you need multiple doc versions:

```txt
docs/
‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ v1.0.0/
‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ getting-started.mdx
‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ v2.0.0/
‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ getting-started.mdx
‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ next/
    ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ getting-started.mdx
```

Set the active version in `specra.config.json`:

```json
{
  "site": {
    "activeVersion": "v2.0.0"
  }
}
```

Users can switch versions with the version dropdown in the UI.

## SEO Best Practices

### Page Titles and Descriptions

Always include both in frontmatter:

```mdx
---
title: Getting Started with Specra
description: Learn how to install and configure Specra for your documentation needs
---
```

### Descriptive Headings

Use clear, descriptive headings that include keywords:

**Good:**
```markdown
## Installing Specra with npm
```

**Bad:**
```markdown
## Installation
```

### Structured Content

Use proper heading hierarchy (h1 ‚Üí h2 ‚Üí h3). Never skip levels.

## Common Patterns

### Prerequisites Section

Start tutorials with prerequisites:

```mdx
## Prerequisites

Before you begin, ensure you have:

- Node.js 18 or higher
- A text editor
- Basic knowledge of Markdown
```

### Step-by-Step Tutorials

Use the Steps component:

```mdx
<Steps>
  <Step title="Install the package">
    Run npm install specra
  </Step>
  <Step title="Configure">
    Create a specra.config.json file
  </Step>
  <Step title="Start the server">
    Run npm run dev
  </Step>
</Steps>
```

### Code with Explanation

Pair code examples with explanations:

```mdx
Configure your site title and description:

```json
{
  "site": {
    "title": "My Docs",
    "description": "Documentation for my project"
  }
}
```

The `title` appears in the browser tab and navigation. The `description` is used for SEO meta tags.
```

### Quick Reference Cards

Use CardGrid for scannable reference sections:

```mdx
<CardGrid cols={3}>
  <Card icon="terminal" title="CLI" description="Command line tools" href="/cli" />
  <Card icon="book" title="Guides" description="Step-by-step tutorials" href="/guides" />
  <Card icon="code" title="API" description="API reference docs" href="/api" />
</CardGrid>
```

  />

# Writing Content in Specra

Specra uses MDX (Markdown + JSX) for documentation, giving you the simplicity of Markdown with the power of React components. This guide covers everything you need to write great documentation.

## MDX Basics

MDX files look like regular Markdown but let you use React components anywhere in your content.

### Standard Markdown

All standard Markdown syntax works as expected:

**Headings:**
```markdown
# Heading 1
## Heading 2
### Heading 3
```

**Text formatting:**
```markdown
**Bold text**
*Italic text*
~~Strikethrough~~
`Inline code`
```

**Lists:**
```markdown
- Unordered list
- Another item
  - Nested item

1. Ordered list
2. Second item
   1. Nested ordered item
```

**Links and images:**
```markdown
[Link text](https://example.com)
![Alt text](/images/photo.png)
```

**Code blocks:**
````markdown
```javascript
function hello() {
  console.log("Hello, world!")
}
```
````

**Tables:**
```markdown
| Column 1 | Column 2 | Column 3 |
|----------|----------|----------|
| Data 1   | Data 2   | Data 3   |
| More     | Info     | Here     |
```

**Blockquotes:**
```markdown
> This is a quote.
> It can span multiple lines.
```

**Horizontal rules:**
```markdown
---
```

## Using Components

Components are used with JSX syntax directly in your MDX:

```mdx
<Callout type="info">
  This is a callout component!
</Callout>
```

All components are automatically available - no imports needed.

### Component Examples

**Alert readers to important information:**
```mdx
<Callout type="warning">
  Make sure to backup your data before proceeding.
</Callout>
```

**Create tabbed content:**
```mdx
<Tabs defaultValue="option1">
  <Tab label="Option 1">
    Content for the first tab
  </Tab>
  <Tab label="Option 2">
    Content for the second tab
  </Tab>
</Tabs>
```

**Guide users through steps:**
```mdx
<Steps>
  <Step title="Install dependencies">
    Run `npm install` to get started.
  </Step>
  <Step title="Configure your app">
    Edit the config file with your settings.
  </Step>
</Steps>
```

See the [Components](/docs/v1.0.0/components) section for all available components.

## Content Organization

### File Structure Best Practices

Organize files logically to make content easy to find:

```txt
docs/v1.0.0/
‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ getting-started.mdx         # Top level: essential pages
‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ installation.mdx
‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ guides/                     # Group related content
‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ _category_.json
‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ basics.mdx
‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ advanced.mdx
‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ examples/              # Further nesting for sub-topics
‚îÇ       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ _category_.json
‚îÇ       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ example-1.mdx
‚îÇ       ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ example-2.mdx
‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ api/
    ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ _category_.json
    ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ reference.mdx
```

**Tips:**
- Keep the top level for critical pages users need first
- Use folders to group related content
- Limit nesting to 2-3 levels max
- Name files descriptively (`authentication.mdx` not `auth.mdx`)

### Controlling Page Order

Use `sidebar_position` in frontmatter to control ordering:

```mdx
---
title: Installation
sidebar_position: 1
---
```

Lower numbers appear first. Pages without a position are sorted alphabetically.

For folders, use `_category_.json`:

```json
{
  "label": "Getting Started",
  "position": 1
}
```

## Writing Style Tips

Good documentation is clear, concise, and helpful. Here are some tips:

### Be Clear and Direct

**Good:**
> Click the "Save" button to save your changes.

**Bad:**
> You might want to consider clicking on the button labeled "Save" if you would like to persist your modifications to storage.

### Use Active Voice

**Good:**
> The system validates your input.

**Bad:**
> Your input is validated by the system.

### Show, Don't Just Tell

Include examples with every concept:

```mdx
## Using Environment Variables

Access environment variables in your config:

```json
{
  "env": {
    "API_URL": "https://api.example.com"
  }
}
```

Then reference them in your MDX:

```mdx
The API is available at {process.env.API_URL}
```
```

### Break Up Long Content

Use headings, lists, callouts, and components to create visual breaks:

```mdx
## Configuration Options

There are several ways to configure authentication:

### API Keys

API keys are simple but less secure.

<Callout type="warning">
  Never commit API keys to version control.
</Callout>

### OAuth 2.0

OAuth provides better security for user-facing apps.

<Steps>
  <Step title="Register your app">
    Create an app in the provider dashboard.
  </Step>
  <Step title="Configure callback URL">
    Set your redirect URI in the app settings.
  </Step>
</Steps>
```

## Working with Images

### Adding Images

Place images in the `public/` folder:

```txt
public/
‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ images/
‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ screenshot.png
‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ diagram.svg
```

Reference them in MDX:

```mdx
![Dashboard screenshot](/images/screenshot.png)
```

### Image Best Practices

**Use descriptive alt text:**
```mdx
![Login form showing email and password fields](/images/login.png)
```

**Optimize image sizes:**
- Use WebP format when possible
- Compress images before adding to repo
- Keep images under 500KB

**Use the Image component for advanced features:**
```mdx
<Image
  src="/images/hero.png"
  alt="Hero image"
  caption="The main dashboard view"
  width={800}
  height={400}
/>
```

## Code Examples

### Syntax Highlighting

Specify the language after the opening backticks:

````markdown
```javascript
const greeting = "Hello, world!"
console.log(greeting)
```

```python
def greet():
    print("Hello, world!")
```

```bash
npm install specra
```
````

Supported languages include: javascript, typescript, python, bash, json, yaml, markdown, html, css, and many more.

### Highlighting Lines

Highlight specific lines to draw attention:

````markdown
```javascript {2,4-6}
function calculateTotal(items) {
  const subtotal = items.reduce((sum, item) => sum + item.price, 0)
  const tax = subtotal * 0.1
  const shipping = 5.99
  const total = subtotal + tax + shipping
  return total
}
```
````

### File Names

Show which file the code belongs to:

````markdown
```javascript title="src/utils.js"
export function formatDate(date) {
  return date.toLocaleDateString()
}
```
````

### Use the CodeBlock Component

For more control:

```mdx
<CodeBlock
  language="javascript"
  title="src/app.js"
  highlightLines={[3, 5]}
  showLineNumbers={true}
>
{`function app() {
  const config = loadConfig()
  const server = createServer(config)
  server.listen(3000)
  console.log("Server running")
}`}
</CodeBlock>
```

## Links and Navigation

### Internal Links

Link to other pages in your docs:

```mdx
See the [Configuration guide](/docs/v1.0.0/configuration/overview) for details.
```

Use relative paths from the site root, including the version.

### External Links

External links open in a new tab automatically:

```mdx
Check out the [Next.js documentation](https://nextjs.org/docs).
```

### Anchor Links

Link to headings on the same page:

```mdx
Jump to [Installation](#installation) below.
```

Heading anchors are auto-generated from the heading text in lowercase with hyphens.

## Frontmatter Reference

Every MDX file needs frontmatter. Here's a complete example:

```mdx
---
title: Advanced Topics
description: Deep dive into advanced Specra features
sidebar_position: 10
tab_group: guides
icon: zap
tags: [advanced, configuration, optimization]
draft: false
---

# Your content starts here
```

**Required fields:**
- `title`: Page title

**Recommended fields:**
- `description`: SEO description (150-160 characters)

**Optional fields:**
- `sidebar_position`: Number for sidebar ordering
- `tab_group`: Assign to a tab group
- `icon`: Lucide icon name
- `tags`: Array of tags
- `draft`: Hide in production if true

## Advanced MDX Features

### Importing Components

While built-in components work automatically, you can import custom ones:

```mdx
import { MyCustomComponent } from '@/components/custom'

<MyCustomComponent data="example" />
```

### Using JavaScript Expressions

Embed JavaScript expressions:

```mdx
The current year is {new Date().getFullYear()}.
```

### Conditional Content

Use JavaScript for conditional rendering:

```mdx
{process.env.NODE_ENV === 'development' && (
  <Callout type="info">
    You're viewing the development version.
  </Callout>
)}
```

## Version Management

When you need multiple doc versions:

```txt
docs/
‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ v1.0.0/
‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ getting-started.mdx
‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ v2.0.0/
‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ getting-started.mdx
‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ next/
    ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ getting-started.mdx
```

Set the active version in `specra.config.json`:

```json
{
  "site": {
    "activeVersion": "v2.0.0"
  }
}
```

Users can switch versions with the version dropdown in the UI.

## SEO Best Practices

### Page Titles and Descriptions

Always include both in frontmatter:

```mdx
---
title: Getting Started with Specra
description: Learn how to install and configure Specra for your documentation needs
---
```

### Descriptive Headings

Use clear, descriptive headings that include keywords:

**Good:**
```markdown
## Installing Specra with npm
```

**Bad:**
```markdown
## Installation
```

### Structured Content

Use proper heading hierarchy (h1 ‚Üí h2 ‚Üí h3). Never skip levels.

## Common Patterns

### Prerequisites Section

Start tutorials with prerequisites:

```mdx
## Prerequisites

Before you begin, ensure you have:

- Node.js 18 or higher
- A text editor
- Basic knowledge of Markdown
```

### Step-by-Step Tutorials

Use the Steps component:

```mdx
<Steps>
  <Step title="Install the package">
    Run npm install specra
  </Step>
  <Step title="Configure">
    Create a specra.config.json file
  </Step>
  <Step title="Start the server">
    Run npm run dev
  </Step>
</Steps>
```

### Code with Explanation

Pair code examples with explanations:

```mdx
Configure your site title and description:

```json
{
  "site": {
    "title": "My Docs",
    "description": "Documentation for my project"
  }
}
```

The `title` appears in the browser tab and navigation. The `description` is used for SEO meta tags.
```

### Quick Reference Cards

Use CardGrid for scannable reference sections:

```mdx
<CardGrid cols={3}>
  <Card icon="terminal" title="CLI" description="Command line tools" href="/cli" />
  <Card icon="book" title="Guides" description="Step-by-step tutorials" href="/guides" />
  <Card icon="code" title="API" description="API reference docs" href="/api" />
</CardGrid>
```

## Next Steps

<CardGrid cols={2}>
  <Card
    icon="palette"
    title="Components"
    description="Explore all available MDX components"
    href="/docs/v1.0.0/components"
  />
  <Card
    icon="settings"
    title="Configuration"
    description="Customize your documentation site"
    href="/docs/v1.0.0/configuration/overview"
  />
</CardGrid>

This page demonstrates automatic API documentation generation from an **OpenAPI 3.0** specification.

The component automatically detects the format and parses it into our documentation system.

<Callout type="info" title="Auto-Detection">
The `ApiReference` component automatically detects OpenAPI format when you use `parser="auto"` (the default).
</Callout>

---

<ApiReference spec="/api-specs/openapi-example.json" />

---

## About This Example

This example shows how the parser handles:

- ‚úÖ **OpenAPI 3.0 format** detection
- ‚úÖ **Schema references** (`$ref`) resolution
- ‚úÖ **Path parameters** (`{id}` converted to `:id`)
- ‚úÖ **Request/Response schemas** with examples
- ‚úÖ **Security schemes** (Bearer tokens, API keys)
- ‚úÖ **Multiple response codes** (success and errors)

## Using Your Own OpenAPI Spec

To use your own OpenAPI specification:

1. **Place your spec file** in the `/public/api-specs/` directory
2. **Reference it in your MDX** file:

```mdx
<ApiReference spec="/api-specs/your-api.json" parser="openapi" />
```

Or let it auto-detect:

```mdx
<ApiReference spec="/api-specs/your-api.json" />
```

The parser supports both **OpenAPI 3.x** and **Swagger 2.0** formats.

# Callout

Callouts draw attention to important information in your documentation. They come in different styles to convey different types of messages, from helpful tips to critical warnings.

## Basic Usage

<Tabs defaultValue="Preview">
  <Tab label="Preview">
<Callout type="info">
  This is helpful information for the reader.
</Callout>
  </Tab>
  <Tab label="Code">
```mdx
<Callout type="info">
  This is helpful information for the reader.
</Callout>
```
  </Tab>
</Tabs>

## Callout Types

Specra includes seven callout types, each with distinct styling:

### Info

<Tabs defaultValue="Preview">
  <Tab label="Preview">
<Callout type="info">
  Provides additional context or helpful information that enhances understanding.
</Callout>
  </Tab>
  <Tab label="Code">
```mdx
<Callout type="info">
  Provides additional context or helpful information.
</Callout>
```
  </Tab>
</Tabs>

### Note

<Tabs defaultValue="Preview">
  <Tab label="Preview">
<Callout type="note">
  Highlights important details the reader should be aware of.
</Callout>
  </Tab>
  <Tab label="Code">
```mdx
<Callout type="note">
  Highlights important details the reader should be aware of.
</Callout>
```
  </Tab>
</Tabs>

### Tip

<Tabs defaultValue="Preview">
  <Tab label="Preview">
<Callout type="tip">
  Offers suggestions for better usage or best practices.
</Callout>
  </Tab>
  <Tab label="Code">
```mdx
<Callout type="tip">
  Offers suggestions for better usage or best practices.
</Callout>
```
  </Tab>
</Tabs>

### Warning

<Tabs defaultValue="Preview">
  <Tab label="Preview">
<Callout type="warning">
  Alerts users to potential issues or breaking changes.
</Callout>
  </Tab>
  <Tab label="Code">
```mdx
<Callout type="warning">
  Alerts users to potential issues or breaking changes.
</Callout>
```
  </Tab>
</Tabs>

### Success

<Tabs defaultValue="Preview">
  <Tab label="Preview">
<Callout type="success">
  Confirms positive outcomes or successfully completed actions.
</Callout>
  </Tab>
  <Tab label="Code">
```mdx
<Callout type="success">
  Confirms positive outcomes or successfully completed actions.
</Callout>
```
  </Tab>
</Tabs>

### Error

<Tabs defaultValue="Preview">
  <Tab label="Preview">
<Callout type="error">
  Highlights critical issues or things users should avoid.
</Callout>
  </Tab>
  <Tab label="Code">
```mdx
<Callout type="error">
  Highlights critical issues or things users should avoid.
</Callout>
```
  </Tab>
</Tabs>

### Danger

<Tabs defaultValue="Preview">
  <Tab label="Preview">
<Callout type="danger">
  Warns about potentially destructive or irreversible actions.
</Callout>
  </Tab>
  <Tab label="Code">
```mdx
<Callout type="danger">
  Warns about potentially destructive or irreversible actions.
</Callout>
```
  </Tab>
</Tabs>

## Props

| Prop | Type | Default | Description |
|------|------|---------|-------------|
| `type` | `string` | `"info"` | Callout style: `info`, `note`, `tip`, `warning`, `success`, `error`, or `danger` |
| `children` | `ReactNode` | Required | The content inside the callout |

## Advanced Examples

### Multi-Line Content

Callouts can contain any MDX content, including formatted text, lists, and code:

<Tabs defaultValue="Preview">
  <Tab label="Preview">
<Callout type="warning">
  **Important considerations before deploying:**

  - Back up your database
  - Test in staging environment first
  - Notify your team about downtime

  Run `npm run db:backup` to create a backup.
</Callout>
  </Tab>
  <Tab label="Code">
```mdx
<Callout type="warning">
  **Important considerations before deploying:**

  - Back up your database
  - Test in staging environment first
  - Notify your team about downtime

  Run `npm run db:backup` to create a backup.
</Callout>
```
  </Tab>
</Tabs>

### Nested Components

You can nest other components inside callouts:

<Tabs defaultValue="Preview">
  <Tab label="Preview">
<Callout type="info">
  **Pro tip:** Use code blocks to show examples

  <Tabs defaultValue="js">
    <Tab label="JavaScript">
      console.log("Hello!")
    </Tab>
    <Tab label="Python">
      print("Hello!")
    </Tab>
  </Tabs>
</Callout>
  </Tab>
  <Tab label="Code">
```mdx
<Callout type="info">
  **Pro tip:** Use code blocks to show examples

  <Tabs defaultValue="js">
    <Tab label="JavaScript">
      console.log("Hello!")
    </Tab>
    <Tab label="Python">
      print("Hello!")
    </Tab>
  </Tabs>
</Callout>
```
  </Tab>
</Tabs>

## GitHub-Style Alerts

Prefer Markdown syntax? Specra also supports GitHub-style alert syntax using blockquotes:

<Tabs defaultValue="Preview">
  <Tab label="Preview">
> [!NOTE]
> This is a note using GitHub-style syntax.

> [!TIP]
> This is a tip using blockquote syntax.

> [!WARNING]
> This is a warning alert.
  </Tab>
  <Tab label="Code">
```markdown
> [!NOTE]
> This is a note using GitHub-style syntax.

> [!TIP]
> This is a tip using blockquote syntax.

> [!WARNING]
> This is a warning alert.
```
  </Tab>
</Tabs>

**Supported alert types:**
- `[!NOTE]` - Same as type="note"
- `[!TIP]` - Same as type="tip"
- `[!IMPORTANT]` - Same as type="warning"
- `[!WARNING]` - Same as type="warning"
- `[!CAUTION]` - Same as type="danger"

## When to Use Each Type

**Info** - Additional context that enhances understanding
- "You can also achieve this using the CLI"
- "This feature is available in v2.0 and later"

**Note** - Important information that shouldn't be skipped
- "This setting affects all users in your organization"
- "Changes take effect after server restart"

**Tip** - Best practices and helpful suggestions
- "For better performance, enable caching"
- "Use TypeScript for better autocomplete"

**Warning** - Potential problems or breaking changes
- "This will modify your database schema"
- "Deprecated in v3.0, use newMethod() instead"

**Success** - Positive confirmations
- "Setup complete! Your site is ready"
- "All tests passed successfully"

**Error** - Critical issues to avoid
- "Do not expose your API key in client code"
- "This operation cannot be undone"

**Danger** - Destructive or irreversible actions
- "This will permanently delete all data"
- "Proceeding will revoke all access tokens"

## Accessibility

Callouts are semantic and accessible:

- Uses appropriate ARIA roles
- Screen reader friendly
- Keyboard navigable
- Color contrast compliant (WCAG AA)
- Icons are decorative with proper alt text

</CardGrid>

      print("Hello!")
    </Tab>
  </Tabs>
</Callout>
  </Tab>
  <Tab label="Code">
```mdx
<Callout type="info">
  **Pro tip:** Use code blocks to show examples

  <Tabs defaultValue="js">
    <Tab label="JavaScript">
      console.log("Hello!")
    </Tab>
    <Tab label="Python">
      print("Hello!")
    </Tab>
  </Tabs>
</Callout>
```
  </Tab>
</Tabs>

## GitHub-Style Alerts

Prefer Markdown syntax? Specra also supports GitHub-style alert syntax using blockquotes:

<Tabs defaultValue="Preview">
  <Tab label="Preview">
> [!NOTE]
> This is a note using GitHub-style syntax.

> [!TIP]
> This is a tip using blockquote syntax.

> [!WARNING]
> This is a warning alert.
  </Tab>
  <Tab label="Code">
```markdown
> [!NOTE]
> This is a note using GitHub-style syntax.

> [!TIP]
> This is a tip using blockquote syntax.

> [!WARNING]
> This is a warning alert.
```
  </Tab>
</Tabs>

**Supported alert types:**
- `[!NOTE]` - Same as type="note"
- `[!TIP]` - Same as type="tip"
- `[!IMPORTANT]` - Same as type="warning"
- `[!WARNING]` - Same as type="warning"
- `[!CAUTION]` - Same as type="danger"

## When to Use Each Type

**Info** - Additional context that enhances understanding
- "You can also achieve this using the CLI"
- "This feature is available in v2.0 and later"

**Note** - Important information that shouldn't be skipped
- "This setting affects all users in your organization"
- "Changes take effect after server restart"

**Tip** - Best practices and helpful suggestions
- "For better performance, enable caching"
- "Use TypeScript for better autocomplete"

**Warning** - Potential problems or breaking changes
- "This will modify your database schema"
- "Deprecated in v3.0, use newMethod() instead"

**Success** - Positive confirmations
- "Setup complete! Your site is ready"
- "All tests passed successfully"

**Error** - Critical issues to avoid
- "Do not expose your API key in client code"
- "This operation cannot be undone"

**Danger** - Destructive or irreversible actions
- "This will permanently delete all data"
- "Proceeding will revoke all access tokens"

## Accessibility

Callouts are semantic and accessible:

- Uses appropriate ARIA roles
- Screen reader friendly
- Keyboard navigable
- Color contrast compliant (WCAG AA)
- Icons are decorative with proper alt text

</CardGrid>
