The Frame component embeds external content securely using iframes.

## Usage

```mdx
<Frame 
  src="https://example.com/embed" 
  title="Embedded Content"
  height={400}
/>
```

## Live Example

<Frame 
  src="https://www.openstreetmap.org/export/embed.html?bbox=-0.1%2C51.5%2C0%2C51.52&layer=mapnik"
  title="OpenStreetMap"
  height={300}
/>

## Props

| Prop | Type | Default | Description |
|------|------|---------|-------------|
| `src` | `string` | required | URL of the content to embed |
| `title` | `string` | `"Embedded content"` | Accessible title for the iframe |
| `height` | `number \| string` | `500` | Height of the iframe |
| `width` | `string` | `"100%"` | Width of the iframe |

## Security

<Callout type="warning">
The Frame component uses a sandboxed iframe with limited permissions for security. Allowed features include: `allow-scripts`, `allow-same-origin`, `allow-forms`, and `allow-popups`.
</Callout>

## Common Use Cases

- Embedding maps (Google Maps, OpenStreetMap)
- Interactive demos and playgrounds
- Third-party widgets
- Code sandboxes (CodeSandbox, StackBlitz)

## Example: CodeSandbox Embed

```mdx
<Frame 
  src="https://codesandbox.io/embed/new?codemirror=1"
  title="CodeSandbox"
  height={500}
/>
```

The Image component displays optimized images with optional captions and zoom-on-click functionality.

## Usage

```mdx
<Image 
  src="/images/screenshot.png" 
  alt="Application screenshot"
  caption="Dashboard overview"
/>
```

## Live Example

<Image 
  src="https://www.kindpng.com/picc/m/160-1609318_document-management-system-png-transparent-png.png" 
  alt="Documentation system illustration"
  caption="Modern documentation platform"
  width={600}
  height={400}
/>

<Image 
  src="/placeholder.svg" 
  alt="Placeholder Image"
  caption="Local placeholder image"
  width={600}
  height={400}
/>

## Props

| Prop | Type | Default | Description |
|------|------|---------|-------------|
| `src` | `string` | required | Image source URL |
| `alt` | `string` | required | Accessible alt text |
| `caption` | `string` | - | Caption displayed below image |
| `width` | `number` | `1200` | Image width |
| `height` | `number` | `675` | Image height |
| `zoom` | `boolean` | `true` | Enable click-to-zoom |

## Features

### Zoom Functionality

<Callout type="info">
Click on any image to view it in a full-screen lightbox. A zoom icon appears on hover.
</Callout>

### Captions

Add context to images with the `caption` prop. Captions are styled italicized and centered below the image.

### Optimization

Images are automatically optimized using Next.js Image component for:
- Lazy loading
- Responsive sizing
- Modern formats (WebP)
- Caching

## Best Practices

- Always provide descriptive `alt` text for accessibility
- Use appropriate `width` and `height` to prevent layout shift
- Add `caption` for complex diagrams or screenshots that need explanation
- Set `zoom={false}` for decorative or small images

56:T797,
The Math component renders mathematical equations using KaTeX, supporting both inline and block math.

## Usage

### Inline Math

```mdx
The equation <Math>{"E = mc^2"}</Math> is famous.
```

### Block Math

```mdx
<Math block>
  {"\\int_{-\\infty}^{\\infty} e^{-x^2} dx = \\sqrt{\\pi}"}
</Math>
```

## Live Examples

### Inline Math

Einstein's famous equation <Math>{"E = mc^2"}</Math> relates energy and mass.

The quadratic formula is <Math>{"x = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2-4ac}}{2a}"}</Math>.

### Block Math

<Math block>
  {"\\int_{-\\infty}^{\\infty} e^{-x^2} dx = \\sqrt{\\pi}"}
</Math>

<Math block>
  {"f(x) = \\frac{1}{\\sigma\\sqrt{2\\pi}} e^{-\\frac{1}{2}\\left(\\frac{x-\\mu}{\\sigma}\\right)^2}"}
</Math>

### Matrix

<Math block>
  {"\\begin{pmatrix} a & b \\\\ c & d \\end{pmatrix}"}
</Math>

### Summation

<Math block>
  {"\\sum_{n=1}^{\\infty} \\frac{1}{n^2} = \\frac{\\pi^2}{6}"}
</Math>

## Props

| Prop | Type | Default | Description |
|------|------|---------|-------------|
| `children` | `string` | required | LaTeX math expression |
| `block` | `boolean` | `false` | Display as block (centered) |

## LaTeX Syntax

<Callout type="tip">
Remember to escape backslashes in JSX. Use `\\` instead of `\` for LaTeX commands.
</Callout>

### Common Symbols

| Symbol | LaTeX | Result |
|--------|-------|--------|
| Greek letters | `\alpha, \beta, \gamma` | <Math>{"\\alpha, \\beta, \\gamma"}</Math> |
| Fractions | `\frac{a}{b}` | <Math>{"\\frac{a}{b}"}</Math> |
| Square root | `\sqrt{x}` | <Math>{"\\sqrt{x}"}</Math> |
| Exponents | `x^{n}` | <Math>{"x^{n}"}</Math> |
| Subscripts | `x_{i}` | <Math>{"x_{i}"}</Math> |
| Infinity | `\infty` | <Math>{"\\infty"}</Math> |
| Sum | `\sum` | <Math>{"\\sum"}</Math> |
| Integral | `\int` | <Math>{"\\int"}</Math> |

## Resources

- [KaTeX Documentation](https://katex.org/docs/supported.html)
- [LaTeX Math Symbols](https://oeis.org/wiki/List_of_LaTeX_mathematical_symbols)
57:T797,
The Math component renders mathematical equations using KaTeX, supporting both inline and block math.

## Usage

### Inline Math

```mdx
The equation <Math>{"E = mc^2"}</Math> is famous.
```

### Block Math

```mdx
<Math block>
  {"\\int_{-\\infty}^{\\infty} e^{-x^2} dx = \\sqrt{\\pi}"}
</Math>
```

## Live Examples

### Inline Math

Einstein's famous equation <Math>{"E = mc^2"}</Math> relates energy and mass.

The quadratic formula is <Math>{"x = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2-4ac}}{2a}"}</Math>.

### Block Math

<Math block>
  {"\\int_{-\\infty}^{\\infty} e^{-x^2} dx = \\sqrt{\\pi}"}
</Math>

<Math block>
  {"f(x) = \\frac{1}{\\sigma\\sqrt{2\\pi}} e^{-\\frac{1}{2}\\left(\\frac{x-\\mu}{\\sigma}\\right)^2}"}
</Math>

### Matrix

<Math block>
  {"\\begin{pmatrix} a & b \\\\ c & d \\end{pmatrix}"}
</Math>

### Summation

<Math block>
  {"\\sum_{n=1}^{\\infty} \\frac{1}{n^2} = \\frac{\\pi^2}{6}"}
</Math>

## Props

| Prop | Type | Default | Description |
|------|------|---------|-------------|
| `children` | `string` | required | LaTeX math expression |
| `block` | `boolean` | `false` | Display as block (centered) |

## LaTeX Syntax

<Callout type="tip">
Remember to escape backslashes in JSX. Use `\\` instead of `\` for LaTeX commands.
</Callout>

### Common Symbols

| Symbol | LaTeX | Result |
|--------|-------|--------|
| Greek letters | `\alpha, \beta, \gamma` | <Math>{"\\alpha, \\beta, \\gamma"}</Math> |
| Fractions | `\frac{a}{b}` | <Math>{"\\frac{a}{b}"}</Math> |
| Square root | `\sqrt{x}` | <Math>{"\\sqrt{x}"}</Math> |
| Exponents | `x^{n}` | <Math>{"x^{n}"}</Math> |
| Subscripts | `x_{i}` | <Math>{"x_{i}"}</Math> |
| Infinity | `\infty` | <Math>{"\\infty"}</Math> |
| Sum | `\sum` | <Math>{"\\sum"}</Math> |
| Integral | `\int` | <Math>{"\\int"}</Math> |

## Diagram Types

Mermaid supports many diagram types:

- **Flowcharts** - `graph TD` or `graph LR`
- **Sequence diagrams** - `sequenceDiagram`
- **Class diagrams** - `classDiagram`
- **State diagrams** - `stateDiagram-v2`
- **Entity Relationship** - `erDiagram`
- **Gantt charts** - `gantt`
- **Pie charts** - `pie`

## Theme Support

<Callout type="info">
Mermaid diagrams automatically adapt to light and dark mode themes.
</Callout>

- [Mermaid Documentation](https://mermaid.js.org/intro/)
- [Live Editor](https://mermaid.live/)

The Steps component creates numbered step-by-step instructions, perfect for tutorials and guides.

## Usage

```mdx
<Steps>
  <Step title="First Step">
    Description of the first step.
  </Step>
  
  <Step title="Second Step">
    Description of the second step.
  </Step>
</Steps>
```

## Live Example

<Steps>
  <Step title="Install Dependencies">
    First, install the required npm packages:
    
```bash
npm install next react react-dom
```
  </Step>
  
  <Step title="Create Configuration">
    Create a configuration file in your project root:
    
```javascript
// next.config.js
module.exports = {
  reactStrictMode: true,
}
```
  </Step>
  
  <Step title="Start Development Server">
    Run the development server:
    
```bash
npm run dev
```
    
Your site is now running at `http://localhost:3000`!
  </Step>
  
  <Step title="Deploy to Production">
    When ready, build and deploy your application:
    
```bash
npm run build
npm start
```
  </Step>
</Steps>

## Props

### Steps

| Prop | Type | Default | Description |
|------|------|---------|-------------|
| `children` | `ReactNode` | required | Step components |

### Step

| Prop | Type | Default | Description |
|------|------|---------|-------------|
| `title` | `string` | required | Step title/heading |
| `children` | `ReactNode` | required | Step content |

## Features

- **Automatic Numbering** - Steps are numbered automatically using CSS counters
- **Visual Timeline** - A connecting line shows the progression through steps
- **Rich Content** - Each step supports full MDX content including code blocks

<Callout type="tip">
Steps work great for installation guides, tutorials, and any sequential process that users need to follow.
</Callout>

```
  </Tab>

  </Tab>

pnpm add my-package
```
  </Tab>

  return `Hello, ${name}!`;
}

  </Tab>

  return `Hello, ${name}!`;

| Prop | Type | Default | Description |
|------|------|---------|-------------|
| `label` | `string` | required | Tab button label |
| `children` | `ReactNode` | required | Content shown when tab is active |

Tooltips display additional information when hovering over an element.

## Usage

```mdx
Hover over <Tooltip content="This is a tooltip!">this text</Tooltip> to see more.
```

## Live Examples

### Basic Tooltip

Hover over <Tooltip content="Additional context appears here">this text</Tooltip> to see a tooltip.

### Different Positions

<Tooltip content="Tooltip on top" position="top">Top</Tooltip> | <Tooltip content="Tooltip on bottom" position="bottom">Bottom</Tooltip> | <Tooltip content="Tooltip on left" position="left">Left</Tooltip> | <Tooltip content="Tooltip on right" position="right">Right</Tooltip>

### With Icons

<Tooltip content="Settings and preferences">
  <Icon icon="settings" size={20} />
</Tooltip> <Tooltip content="Get help">
  <Icon icon="help-circle" size={20} />
</Tooltip> <Tooltip content="More information">
  <Icon icon="info" size={20} />
</Tooltip>

### In Context

This feature is <Badge variant="success">New</Badge>{' '}
<Tooltip content="Added in version 2.0">
  <Icon icon="info" size={14} />
</Tooltip>

## Props

| Prop | Type | Default | Description |
|------|------|---------|-------------|
| `children` | `ReactNode` | required | Element that triggers tooltip |
| `content` | `string` | required | Tooltip text content |
| `position` | `"top" \| "bottom" \| "left" \| "right"` | `"top"` | Tooltip position |

## Best Practices

<Callout type="tip">
- Keep tooltip content concise (1-2 sentences max)
- Use for supplementary information, not critical content
- Ensure the trigger element is focusable for keyboard users
</Callout>

## Common Patterns

### Help Icons

Add small help icons next to form labels or features:

```mdx
**Email** <Tooltip content="We'll never share your email">
  <Icon icon="help-circle" size={14} />
</Tooltip>
```

### Abbreviations

Explain abbreviations inline:

```mdx
The <Tooltip content="Application Programming Interface">API</Tooltip> is well documented.
```

The <Tooltip content="Application Programming Interface">API</Tooltip> is well documented.

60:T6a2,
The Video component embeds videos from local files or popular platforms like YouTube and Vimeo.

## Usage

### YouTube Video

```mdx
<Video 
  src="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=dQw4w9WgXcQ"
  caption="Example video"
/>
```

### Local Video

```mdx
<Video 
  src="/videos/demo.mp4"
  caption="Product demo"
  controls
  poster="/videos/poster.jpg"
/>
```

## Live Examples

### YouTube Embed

<Video 
  src="https://youtu.be/puRFmqfVlLk"
  caption="YouTube video embed example"
  muted
  autoplay
/>

## Props

| Prop | Type | Default | Description |
|------|------|---------|-------------|
| `src` | `string` | required | Video URL (YouTube, Vimeo, or local path) |
| `caption` | `string` | - | Caption below the video |
| `autoplay` | `boolean` | `false` | Auto-play video on load |
| `loop` | `boolean` | `false` | Loop video playback |
| `muted` | `boolean` | `false` | Mute video audio |
| `controls` | `boolean` | `true` | Show video controls |
| `poster` | `string` | - | Poster image URL (local videos only) |

## Supported Platforms

### YouTube

Supports various YouTube URL formats:
- `https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=VIDEO_ID`
- `https://youtu.be/VIDEO_ID`

### Vimeo

Supports Vimeo URLs:
- `https://vimeo.com/VIDEO_ID`

### Local Files

Supports standard video formats:
- MP4 (`.mp4`)
- WebM (`.webm`)
- Ogg (`.ogg`)

## Tips

<Callout type="warning">
Autoplay is often blocked by browsers unless the video is also muted. For auto-playing videos, use both `autoplay` and `muted`:

```mdx
<Video src="/videos/animation.mp4" autoplay muted loop />
```
</Callout>

<Callout type="tip">
Use the `poster` prop for local videos to show a preview image before the video loads.
</Callout>

62:T1add,
Tab groups allow you to organize your documentation into different sections accessible through tabs at the top of your documentation pages. This is particularly useful for separating different types of content like SDK docs, API references, and guides.

## Overview

Tab groups provide a sticky navigation bar that:
- Sits below the header
- Filters sidebar content based on the active tab
- Persists across page navigation
- Supports icons from Lucide React
- Maintains auto-generated sidebar structure

## Configuration

Define tab groups in your `specra.config.json`:

```json
{
  "navigation": {
    "tabGroups": [
      {
        "id": "sdk",
        "label": "SDK Documentation",
        "icon": "code"
      },
      {
        "id": "api",
        "label": "API Reference",
        "icon": "zap"
      },
      {
        "id": "guides",
        "label": "Guides",
        "icon": "book-open"
      }
    ]
  }
}
```

### Tab Group Properties

| Property | Type | Required | Description |
|----------|------|----------|-------------|
| `id` | string | Yes | Unique identifier for the tab group |
| `label` | string | Yes | Display text for the tab |
| `icon` | string | No | Lucide icon name (e.g., "code", "zap", "book-open") |

## Assigning Content to Tabs

There are two ways to assign content to tab groups:

### 1. File-Level Assignment

Add `tab_group` to the frontmatter of your MDX files:

```mdx
---
title: Getting Started
description: Quick start guide
tab_group: guides
---

# Getting Started

Your content here...
```

### 2. Folder-Level Assignment

Add `tab_group` to your `_category_.json` file to assign all files in that folder:

```json
{
  "label": "Components",
  "position": 2,
  "collapsible": true,
  "collapsed": false,
  "icon": "grid",
  "tab_group": "sdk"
}
```

All files within this folder will automatically inherit the `sdk` tab group.

## Behavior and Rules

### Default Tab Assignment

Files without a `tab_group` specified will automatically appear in the **first tab group** defined in your config.

### Precedence

File-level `tab_group` in frontmatter takes precedence over folder-level assignment from `_category_.json`.

### Tab Persistence

The active tab persists when:
- Navigating between pages within the same tab group
- Manually switching tabs
- Clicking links to pages in different tab groups (tab switches automatically)

### Initial Tab Selection

When you land on a page:
- The tab automatically switches to match the page's tab group
- On page reload, the tab reflects the current page's group
- Manual tab selection is preserved when navigating within the same group

## Best Practices

### 1. Logical Grouping

Group related content together:
- **SDK/Library docs**: Installation, configuration, API reference
- **API docs**: REST endpoints, GraphQL schemas, webhooks
- **Guides**: Tutorials, how-tos, best practices

### 2. Consistent Naming

Use clear, concise labels:
- ‚úÖ "SDK Documentation", "API Reference", "Guides"
- ‚ùå "Docs1", "Section A", "Misc"

### 3. Meaningful Icons

Choose icons that represent the content:
- `code` for SDK/library documentation
- `zap` for API references
- `book-open` for guides and tutorials
- `rocket` for getting started content

### 4. Limit Tab Count

Keep the number of tabs manageable:
- **Recommended**: 2-4 tabs
- **Maximum**: 5-6 tabs
- Too many tabs can overwhelm users

## Examples

### Example 1: Simple SDK + API Split

```json
{
  "navigation": {
    "tabGroups": [
      {
        "id": "sdk",
        "label": "SDK",
        "icon": "code"
      },
      {
        "id": "api",
        "label": "API",
        "icon": "zap"
      }
    ]
  }
}
```

### Example 2: Comprehensive Documentation

```json
{
  "navigation": {
    "tabGroups": [
      {
        "id": "getting-started",
        "label": "Getting Started",
        "icon": "rocket"
      },
      {
        "id": "sdk",
        "label": "SDK Reference",
        "icon": "code"
      },
      {
        "id": "api",
        "label": "API Reference",
        "icon": "server"
      },
      {
        "id": "guides",
        "label": "Guides",
        "icon": "book-open"
      }
    ]
  }
}
```

## Advanced Usage

### Nested Folders

Tab groups work seamlessly with nested folder structures:

```txt
docs/v1.0.0/
‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ components/              # tab_group: sdk
‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ _category_.json
‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ button.mdx
‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ input.mdx
‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ api/                     # tab_group: api
‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ _category_.json
‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ authentication.mdx
‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ endpoints.mdx
‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ guides/                  # tab_group: guides
    ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ _category_.json
    ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ quickstart.mdx       # Can override with file-level tab_group
```

### Mixed Tab Groups in Same Folder

You can have files in the same folder belong to different tabs:

```txt
docs/v1.0.0/
‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ _category_.json          # Default: tab_group: sdk
‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ overview.mdx             # Inherits: sdk
‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ api-overview.mdx         # Override: tab_group: api
‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ tutorial.mdx             # Override: tab_group: guides
```

## Troubleshooting

### Tab Not Showing

**Problem**: Tab group defined but not visible

**Solutions**:
- Ensure at least one file is assigned to that tab group
- Check that the tab group `id` matches exactly in both config and frontmatter
- Verify `navigation.tabGroups` is defined in `specra.config.json`

### Content Appearing in Wrong Tab

**Problem**: Page shows up under incorrect tab

**Solutions**:
- Check file-level frontmatter for `tab_group` override
- Verify folder-level `_category_.json` has correct `tab_group`
- Remember: frontmatter takes precedence over `_category_.json`

### Tab Not Persisting

**Problem**: Tab resets when navigating

**Solutions**:
- This is expected behavior when navigating to a page in a different tab group
- The tab automatically switches to match the current page's group
- Manual selection persists only when navigating within the same tab group

## Comparison with Alternatives

### vs. Mintlify/Docusaurus

Unlike Mintlify and Docusaurus which require manual sidebar configuration, our tab groups:
- ‚úÖ Auto-generate sidebar structure from folder hierarchy
- ‚úÖ Support both file and folder-level assignments
- ‚úÖ Persist tab state across navigation
- ‚úÖ Automatically filter sidebar content
- ‚úÖ Require minimal configuration

### Advantages

1. **Auto-generation**: No need to manually maintain sidebar structure
2. **Flexibility**: File-level overrides for granular control
3. **Persistence**: Smart tab state management
4. **Icons**: Built-in icon support from Lucide React
5. **Sticky Navigation**: Tabs stay visible while scrolling

## Related

- [Sidebar Configuration](/docs/v1.0.0/sidebar-configuration)
- [Navigation Settings](/docs/v1.0.0/configuration)
- [Folder Structure](/docs/v1.0.0/folder-structure)
63:T1add,
Tab groups allow you to organize your documentation into different sections accessible through tabs at the top of your documentation pages. This is particularly useful for separating different types of content like SDK docs, API references, and guides.

## Overview

Tab groups provide a sticky navigation bar that:
- Sits below the header
- Filters sidebar content based on the active tab
- Persists across page navigation
- Supports icons from Lucide React
- Maintains auto-generated sidebar structure

## Configuration

Define tab groups in your `specra.config.json`:

```json
{
  "navigation": {
    "tabGroups": [
      {
        "id": "sdk",
        "label": "SDK Documentation",
        "icon": "code"
      },
      {
        "id": "api",
        "label": "API Reference",
        "icon": "zap"
      },
      {
        "id": "guides",
        "label": "Guides",
        "icon": "book-open"
      }
    ]
  }
}
```

| Property | Type | Required | Description |
